  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>So the near-final piece of this puzzle is to make solr.xml be storable in Zookeeper. Code-wise in terms of Solr, this doesn't look very difficult, I'm working on it now.</p> 
                  <p>More interesting is how to get the configuration into ZK in the first place, enhancements to ZkCli? Or boostrap-conf? Other? I'm punting on that for this patch.</p> 
                  <p>Second level is how to tell Solr to get the file from ZK. Some possibilities:</p> 
                  <p>1&gt; A system prop, -DzkSolrXmlPath=blah where blah is the path <em>on zk</em> where the file is. Would require -DzkHost or -DzkRun as well.<br> &gt; pros - simple, I can wrap my head around it.</p> 
                  <ul class="alternate" type="square"> 
                   <li>easy to script<br> &gt; cons - can't run multiple JVMs pointing to different files. Is this really a problem?</li> 
                  </ul> 
                  <p>2&gt; New solr.xml element. Something like:<br> &lt;solr&gt;<br> &lt;solrcloud&gt;<br> &lt;str name="zkHost"&gt;zkurl&lt;/str&gt;<br> &lt;str name="zkSolrXmlPath"&gt;whatever&lt;/str&gt;<br> &lt;/solrcloud&gt;<br> &lt;solr&gt;<br> Really, this form would hinge on the presence or absence of zkSolrXmlPath. If present, go up and look for the indicated solr.xml file on ZK. Any properties in the ZK version would overwrite anything in the local copy.</p> 
                  <p>NOTE: I'm really not very interested in supporting this as an option for old-style solr.xml unless it's <em>really</em> easy. For instance, what if the local solr.xml is new-style and the one in ZK is old-style? Or vice-versa? Since old-style is going away, this doesn't seem like it's worth the effort.</p> 
                  <p>pros - No new mechanisms<br> cons - once again requires that there be a solr.xml file on each client. Admittedly for installations that didn't care much about multiple JVMs, it could be a stock file that didn't change...</p> 
                  <p>For now, I'm going to just manually push solr.xml to ZK, then read it based on a sysprop. That'll get the structure in place while we debate. Not going to check this in until there's some consensus though.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-04-16T18:17:46+0000\'\u003e16\\/Apr\\/13 18:17\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eMy head\'s exploding. We have two files, solr.xml and solr.properties, plus the absence of either. Stored either locally or on ZK. What\'s the precedence here? I vote that solr.properties be only local.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo, some straw-man rules....\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e&gt; solr.properties is irrelevant without a solr.xml, it\'s used only to sub in ${} type constructs.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e&gt; solr.properties can exists only locally. Don\'t look on ZK under any conditions. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e&gt; solr.properties definitions take precedence over \u003cem\u003eany\u003c\\/em\u003e definitions in solr.xml either local or from ZK.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eNote: my objection to making it possible to store solr.properties in ZK is that it complexifies things and one can centrally store a complete solr.xml file there just as easily. I can be persuaded otherwise, but I want a real use case not a theoretical one. We can always add that on later too. Except how does this play when creating collections? I guess that\'s irrelevant, the solr home is what counts.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e&gt; if solr.xml is local, we look for one on ZK iff zkSolrXmlPath is defined (in solr.xml or as a sysprop). Overlay the local one if so. Then apply solr.properties to the combined solr.xml\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e&gt; if no solr.xml is found locally but zkRun or zkHost is defined (sys props), then look in ZK(root or sysprop zkSolrXmlPath) for solr.xml and use that. Overlay with local solr.properties if present.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003col\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eSo the multiple war in single JVM case is handled; you don\'t have to have any sysprops if you have a solr.xml\\/solr.properties pair defined in solrhome for each war. And you can still define a minimal file that just points to ZK for the \\\"real\\\" solr.xml file.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ol\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003col\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eThe no-local-config case is handled by deciding to NOT have a solr.xml locally, set the necessary sysprops (zkhost and possibly zkSolrXmlPath. With or without a solr.properties file.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ol\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003col\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eThe mixed case is handled by having remote solr.xml but local solr.properties in each solrhome to override values.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ol\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"erickerickson\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13633123_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=erickerickson\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"erickerickson\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Erick Erickson\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13633123_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'16\\/Apr\\/13 18:17\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-04-16T18:17:46+0000\'\u003e16\\/Apr\\/13 18:17\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    My head\'s exploding. We have two files, solr.xml and solr.properties, plus the absence of either. Stored either locally or on ZK. What\'s the precedence here? I vote that solr.properties be only local. \\n\\n So, some straw-man rules.... \\n\\n &gt; solr.properties is irrelevant without a solr.xml, it\'s used only to sub in ${} type constructs. \\n\\n &gt; solr.properties can exists only locally. Don\'t look on ZK under any conditions.  \\n\\n &gt; solr.properties definitions take precedence over  any  definitions in solr.xml either local or from ZK. \\n\\n Note: my objection to making it possible to store solr.properties in ZK is that it complexifies things and one can centrally store a complete solr.xml file there just as easily. I can be persuaded otherwise, but I want a real use case not a theoretical one. We can always add that on later too. Except how does this play when creating collections? I guess that\'s irrelevant, the solr home is what counts. \\n\\n &gt; if solr.xml is local, we look for one on ZK iff zkSolrXmlPath is defined (in solr.xml or as a sysprop). Overlay the local one if so. Then apply solr.properties to the combined solr.xml \\n\\n &gt; if no solr.xml is found locally but zkRun or zkHost is defined (sys props), then look in ZK(root or sysprop zkSolrXmlPath) for solr.xml and use that. Overlay with local solr.properties if present. \\n\\n \\n\\t So the multiple war in single JVM case is handled; you don\'t have to have any sysprops if you have a solr.xml\\/solr.properties pair defined in solrhome for each war. And you can still define a minimal file that just points to ZK for the \\\"real\\\" solr.xml file. \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t The no-local-config case is handled by deciding to NOT have a solr.xml locally, set the necessary sysprops (zkhost and possibly zkSolrXmlPath. With or without a solr.properties file. \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t The mixed case is handled by having remote solr.xml but local solr.properties in each solrhome to override values. \\n \\n How do we get it there in the first place? Here\'s what I\'m thinking; it should be possible to just install a stock solr with \u003cem\u003eno\u003c\\/em\u003e modifications on a node, fire it up \u003cem\u003ewithout\u003c\\/em\u003e having any a-priori files and be done with it. (I\'m over-stating the case here, but....)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI want to say \\\"java -DzkHost=blah -jar start.jar\\\" and be done with it. If we require the \\\"correct\\\" solr.properties file to be there why don\'t we just require the correct solr.xml and not bother with a properties file? (I\'m over-stating the case here, but....) \\n\\n I want to say \\\"java -DzkHost=blah -jar start.jar\\\" and be done with it. I\'m probably missing something, but any time we require local files (in this case solr.properties), whether an installation uses any of the auto-config tools or not, it seems like the same problem as requiring the \\\"right\\\" version of solr.xml. \\n\\n Or is this just one of those cases where I\'m over-thinking it and I should just get over it and assume anyone who wants all this flexibility is \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhat are the cons to always using ZK?\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI missed this question from Erik when I was looking earlier.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe primary problem I see with always using zookeeper takes a little explanation.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIn a non-ZK install, making Solr fault tolerant for queries is fairly easy - fire up another node and set up replication.  That\'s not true fault tolerance, as we all know.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eRunning the embedded zookeeper is something we don\'t recommend to people except for single-server proof of concept setups.  I don\'t even know if it\'s possible to set up a fully functional fault-tolerant ensemble using the embedded zookeeper.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eUnfortunately, setting up a standalone ensemble is not trivial.  It\'s not HARD, but when you go from just running \\\"java -jar start.jar\\\" on a single server to a real-world SolrCloud, either you have to start over or you end up performing arcane rituals to migrate your existing setup.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIn my opinion, it is a generally bad idea to have step-by-step documentation that results in a setup that isn\'t fault tolerant.  I have used a lot of open source software with documentation like this.  If documentation about adding redundancy exists, it is often found in a completely different location as reference material, not step-by-step instructions.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOur SolrCloud examples encourage setting up separate Solr JVMs on the same server with the embedded zookeeper.  Because that\'s the available documentation, there are probably production installs set up this way.  I think that kind of setup should be in footnotes or appendices, and the main examples should be multi-node, with clear instructions about how to make sure it won\'t break when something fails.  I\'m not sure how to make it easy to set up zookeeper.  Cross-platform scripting is not easy, especially when one of those platforms is Windows.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"elyograg\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13634473_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=elyograg\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"elyograg\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Shawn Heisey\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13634473_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'17\\/Apr\\/13 21:42\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-04-17T21:42:07+0000\'\u003e17\\/Apr\\/13 21:42\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     What are the cons to always using ZK?  \\n\\n I missed this question from Erik when I was looking earlier. \\n\\n The primary problem I see with always using zookeeper takes a little explanation. \\n\\n In a non-ZK install, making Solr fault tolerant for queries is fairly easy - fire up another node and set up replication.  That\'s not true fault tolerance, as we all know. \\n\\n Running the embedded zookeeper is something we don\'t recommend to people except for single-server proof of concept setups.  I don\'t even know if it\'s possible to set up a fully functional fault-tolerant ensemble using the embedded zookeeper.   \\n\\n Unfortunately, setting up a standalone ensemble is not trivial.  It\'s not HARD, but when you go from just running \\\"java -jar start.jar\\\" on a single server to a real-world SolrCloud, either you have to start over or you end up performing arcane rituals to migrate your existing setup. \\n\\n In my opinion, it is a generally bad idea to have step-by-step documentation that results in a setup that isn\'t fault tolerant.  I have used a lot of open source software with documentation like this.  If documentation about adding redundancy exists, it is often found in a completely different location as reference material, not step-by-step instructions. \\n\\n Our SolrCloud examples encourage setting up separate Solr JVMs on the same server with the embedded zookeeper.  Because that\'s the available documentation, there are probably production installs set up this way.  I think that kind of setup should be in footnotes or appendices, and the main examples should be multi-node, with clear instructions about how to make sure it won\'t break when something fails.  I\'m not sure how to make it easy to set up zookeeper.  Cross-platform scripting is not easy, especially when one of those platforms is Windows.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n
